ARIE 1915-1916 [vol. 038]


A.--List of copper-plates examined during 1915-16.


ARIE/1915-1916/A/1915-16/1 (page 9)
Placement
The trustee of the Veṅkaṭēś-vara temple at Nandyal (Kurnool district).
Dynasty
Vijayanagara
King
Vīrapratāpa Śrīraṅgarāya-dēva-Mahārāya, ruling from Penugoṇḍa.
Date
Śaka 1569, Sarvajit, Vaiśākha, śu. 15.
Language
Telugu
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
South-Indian Inscriptions.
Remarks
Registers that, for the merit of Hazarati Khāna Khāna-Sāhēbulavāru, the nāḍigēru, sthaḷa-paṭṭaṇa-reḍḍis, tōṁṭa-śeṭṭis and karaṇams of the Peda-Nandyāla-śīma included in Peḍakaṇṭi-śīma, granted to a certain Timmaya, the son of chapparam-dāsari Saruvaya, specified contribution of fees from the several professional com-munities of Nandyāla and from about 70 villages of the same sīma for conducting the chapparam-service of the god Veṅ-kaṭēśa.
ARIE/1915-1916/A/1915-16/2 (page 9)
Placement
Do. do.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Do. do.
Date
Do.
Language
Telugu
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
South-Indian Inscriptions.
Remarks
This is a duplicate of No. 1 with a differ-ence in the order in which the several villages are mentioned and in the amounts of contributions.
ARIE/1915-1916/A/1915-16/3 (page 9)
Placement
M.R.Ry. Jarubula Venkates-varlu, village munsif, San-taravuru, (Bapatla taluk, Guntūr district).
Dynasty
Pallava
King
Mahārāja Vijaya-Skandavar-man (II).
Date
33rd year of reign; Hēman-ta-paksha, tṛitīyā trayō-daśī.
Language
Sanskṛit (in Telugu)
Origin
The plates will be acquired for the museum.
Edition
South-Indian Inscriptions.
Remarks
Records that the king gave to Gōlaśarman of the Kāśyapa-gōtra, the village of O1ṁgōḍu in Karmm[ā]-rāshṭra as a brahma-dēya with the 18 kinds of exemptions.
ARIE/1915-1916/A/1915-16/4 (page 9)
Placement
Do. do.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Pallava-Dharma-Mahārāja Simhavarman.
Date
4th year of reign; Vaiśā-kha, śu[kla]-paksha, pañ chami.
Language
Sanskṛit (in Telugu)
Origin
The plates will be acquired for the museum.
Edition
South-Indian Inscriptions.
Remarks
Registers that the king gave on the occa-sion of the grahaṇa (eclipse), the village of O1ṁgōḍu in Karmmā-rāshṭra, to a certain Dēvaśarman who was a resident of Kuṇḍūr and belonged to the Kāśyapa-gōtra.
ARIE/1915-1916/A/1915-16/5 (page 9)
Placement
M.R.Ry. Javvadi Nagayya, Edavalli (Narasaraopet taluk, Guntūr district).
Dynasty
Kōṭa
King
Mahāmaṇḍalēśvara Manma, Manma-Kēta or Kōṭa-Kēta, (i.e., Kēta III), ‘lord of the city of Dhānyakaṭaka.’
Date
Śaka 1162, Māgha, Ardhō-daya.
Language
Sanskṛit & Telugu
Origin
The plates will be acquired for the museum.
Edition
South-Indian Inscriptions.
Remarks
Registers that the king made a gift of the village Eḍavalli which was 300 khaṇḍu-kas in extent, dividing it equally among the Brāhmaṇas of both the Shaṭsahasra country and the Vēṅgī country. Gifts of land in the village were also made to certain temples.
ARIE/1915-1916/A/1915-16/6 (page 9)
Placement
The priest of the Mukhaliṅga-svāmin temple at Muktes-varam (same taluk and district).
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Śaka 1712, Saumya, Āshāḍha, śu. 15.
Language
Telugu
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
…
Remarks
Registers that, for the daily worship and offerings of the god Parasavēdēśvarasvāmin at Chennupalle, the kāpus and karaṇams of that village, with the sanction of the Mahārājaśrī Hanarabbul-Kumpinī (i.e. the Honourable East India Company) according to the Sanad of the prosperous Mr. Rao and with the consent of Rājaśrī Guṇṭupalli Narasiṅgarāyaniṅgāru gave 4 gorrus of land together with their own śelagamēras.
ARIE/1915-1916/A/1915-16/7 (page 9)
Placement
M.R.Ry. Rama Reddi, village munsif of Dayyamdinne (Adōni taluk, Bellary district).
Dynasty
Western Chalukya.
King
Vinayāditya Satyāśraya
Date
Śaka 614, ex-pired; 12th year of reign current; Āshāḍha, full-moon, summer solstice (dak-shiṇāyana).
Language
Sanskṛit (in Kanarese)
Origin
The plates will be acquired for the museum.
Edition
South-Indian Inscriptions.
Remarks
Registers that, at the request of a certain Marddakāri, the king while camping at Taḷayakhēṭa-grāma, made a gift of 200 nivartanas of land on the eastern and southern sides of the village of Uḷchaḍ in Naḷavāḍi-vishaya, to four Brāhmaṇas. Taḷayakhēṭa is stated to have been situated near to the north bank of the river Tagara.

B.--Stone inscriptions copied in 1915 (continued from last Annual Report).

ARIE/1915-1916/B/1915/182 (page 17)
Placement
On the same wall
Dynasty
Chōḷa
King
Rājakēsarivarman alias Vīrarājēndradēva
Date
5th year and 348th day.
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Registers an order of the king assigning the taxes of Vayalaikkāvūr in Kāliyūr-koṭṭam as a tax-free dēvadāna, to meet the requirements of the temple of Mahā-Vishṇukkaḷ at Tirumukkūḍal in Madhurān-taka-chaturvēdimaṅgalam a free village in Kaḷat-tūr-kōṭṭam a sub-division of Jayaṅgoṇdaśōḻa-maṇ-ḍalam. Mentions a number of officers of the king and the seat called Rājēndraśōḻa-Māvalivāṇarājaṉ in the palace Śōḻakēraḷan-tirumāḷigai at Gaṅgai-koṇḍaśōḻapuram. Details of the equipment of a hospital (ātula-śālai or aturaśālā), a school and its pupils connected with the temple, are also given.
ARIE/1915-1916/B/1915/183 (page 17)
Placement
Do.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Parakēsarivarman alias Uḍaiyār śrī-Rājēn-dra-chōḷadēva.
Date
16th year and 32nd day.
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Registers an agreement entered into by certain Vaikhānasas of the temple to use the surplus paddy due by them which had been discovered by an enquiry into the accounts of the temple, for recit-ing the tiruppadiyam in the temple, for the first time. Mentions Śembiyaṉmahādēvi-perumaṇḍa-pam in the middle of the village of Madhurāntaka-chaturvēdimaṅgalam.
ARIE/1915-1916/B/1915/184 (page 17)

ARIE/1915-1916/B/1915/293 (page 26)
Placement
On a Nāga-pillar set up in front of the Rāmaliṅgasvāmin temple on the hill at Ikkurru.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Śaka 10[8]8, Āśvayuja, śu. 10, Thursday.
Language
Telugu
Remarks
Registers that, for the merit of the Mahāmaṇḍalēś-vara Kulōttuṅga-Rājēndra-Chōḍerāja, a certain Malli-Nāyaka gave 3 kha. of (dry) land and 2 martus of wet land, for offerings and 1 kha. of land with two cows and 55 sheep for a perpetual lamp, to the god Mallikhārjuna consecrated by him on the hill at Ikkūru. Records also a gift to the same temple by the chief, Mahāmaṇḍalēśvara Mallayadēva-Mahārāja.

Lost
Language
Telugu
Remarks
Damaged. ARIE/1915-1916/B/1915/299 (page 27)
Placement
On the broken Garuḍa-pillar of the same temple.
Dynasty
Kōṭa
King
Bhīma, husband of Sōmāmbā or Sōmaladēvī.
Date
Śaka 1187, Phāl-guṇa, śu. 5, [Thursday].
Language
Sanskṛit & Telugu
Remarks
Beginning lost and much damaged. Registers the genealogy of a Brahman family of ministers who served under the Kōṭa kings of Dhānyakaṭaka. Vallabha, the minister of Kōṭa-Bhīma established at R6ompicheṟuvu (Paṅkataṭākapura) the temple of Ananta-Gōpinātha in the name and for the merit of his deceased father Ananta. Gifts of lands, wells and tolls are also recorded. The first few lines state that the gifts were made for the victorious rule of Mallaya-Nāyaka, son of Jāyapa-Nāyuḍu.

ARIE/1915-1916/B/1915/316 (page 28)
Placement
On a Nāga-pillar set up in front of the Chandraśēkharasvāmin temple at Tan-gedumalle.
Dynasty
Telugu-Chōḍa
King
Mahāmaṇḍalēśvara Kannāradēva-Chōḍa, son of Kāma-Chōḍa.
Date
Śaka 1037, Jaya, Chaitra, solar eclipse.
Language
Sanskṛit & Telugu
Remarks
Registers that the hereditary minister Māra, son of Īśvara-Nāyaka, dug two tanks at Koppagrāma on the eastern side of Śrīśaila and built also a temple of Sōmēśvara. Chōḍa-Ballidēva, the younger brother of Kannāradēva, gave to that temple the village Biḍepalli close to Koppara (i.e. Koppagrāma, mentioned above). A certain Rudraya-Nāyaka, son of Guṇasāgara and the sēnāpati of Prō[la*] is stated to have confirmed the grant of this village and to have established in the same temple a certain Kāmaya-Paṇḍita who was well versed in the Śaivā-gama.

ARIE/1915-1916/B/1915/326 (page 29)
Placement
On a pillar in the Kalyāṇa-maṇḍapa of the Kōdaṇḍarāmasvāmin temple at Kopparam.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Śaka 1245, Rudhirōdgārin, Chaitra, ba. 3, Mēsha-Saṅk-rānti.
Language
Telugu
Remarks
Registers the gift of voluntary contributions by the Kōmaṭi merchants, oil-mongers, Brāhmaṇas and the professionals of Koppara, for the upkeep of worship in the Varada-Gōpinātha temple at that village. The gift was made for the merit of king Pratāpa-Rudradēva-Mahārāja and his officers (lēmka).
ARIE/1915-1916/B/1915/327 (page 30)
Placement
On the Nāga-pillar set up in front of the same temple.
Dynasty
Telugu-Chōḍa
King
Mahāmaṇḍalēśvara Kannaradēva-Chōḍa
Date
Śaka 1037, Jaya, Chaitra, solar eclipse.
Language
Sanskṛit (in Telugu).
Remarks
Registers that Māra, son of Īśvara-Nāyaka the here-ditary minister of the king, constructed two big tanks, built a temple for Sōmēśvara and a pond at Koppara-grāma. The king visited the god Sōmēś-vara and granted to him the village Koppara-grāma; so also prince Chōḍa-Balli, the younger brother of the king, gave Biḍepalli near Koppara. The grants were confirmed by the Mahāmaṇḍalēś-vara Kaḍiyarāja, a subordinate of Vishṇuvardhana, at the request of Māra. The Kāḷāmukha ascetic Mallikārjuna of Pālūru was placed in charge of the Sōmeśvara temple. On another face of the same pillar are recorded gifts of lamps evidently to the same temple and of sheep required to maintain these lamps.

Remarks
Registers that for the merit of the king Rudradēva Sāmanta Pōti-Nāyuṇḍu constructed the temple of Sūrēśvara in the name of his father at Rāvūru and built the trikūṭa shrines and maṇ-ḍapas. He also gave some wet land for offerings in a village in Anumakoṇḍi-nāḍu. A garden with various fruit trees and flower-plants was also presented. The inscribed pillar was set up at the instance of Pōtaya and Māraya the sons of Pōti-nēḍu who receive a long list of birudas.

Records that the great men of Bhikshāvṛitti-[maṭha] at Śrīśaila and other places, having deputed the voḍeyas and bhaktas, these met at the pavilion of the Vīrēśvara temple at Drōṇādula. At that time the three Vīrapurāntakas, Kōtavīrayya and two others with the consent of the assembly granted the subscriptions which they had the right to collect from the tambaḷas, to the Vīrēśvara temple, for offerings and lamps.

Placement

Dynasty
Do.
King
Chōḍa (son of) Velanāṇṭi Goṅka II
Date
Śaka 1054, Kārttika, śuddha 13, Sunday.
Language
Telugu (verse & prose)
Remarks
Begins with the eulogy of a certain Kāpa of the fourth caste. Mentions Buddhavarma who con-ferred the insignia of royalty on Siṇḍapa-Nāyaka. The grandsons of the latter served under Maṇḍa and gained a victory at Mannēru on behalf of their overlord, and received from him the villages Tūmbaṟṟu and Ātukūru. Next came Kāpana who served under Chōḍa (son of) Velanāṇṭi Goṅka and set up the temple of Mahēśvara at Tūmbaṟṟu. He gave to that temple, named Bhīmēśvara, land which included shares for the several services, the writer of the record, Brāhmaṇas, etc.

Chāḷukya Vik-rama year, 32, Sarvajit, Pushya, Full-moon (Puṇ-ṇami), Tues-day, lunar eclipse.
Language
Kanarese
Remarks
Registers that the chief queen Maleyamatidēvī, at the request of the Daṇḍanāyaka Śrīdharayya, gave to the 140 mahājanas of Tumbuḷa (in Sindavāḍi-nāḍu) which belonged to her, 30 gadyāṇas of gold from the Siddhāya of that village for the maintenance of the commentator (on Śāstras), the reader of the Purāṇas, the teacher of the Ṛig-Vēda and the Yajur-Vēda and of the Brāhmana in charge of the Agnishṭage.
ARIE/1915-1916/B/1915/519 (page 50)
Placement
On a slab set up near the manure-pit of Rāchappa in the same village.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Tribhuvanamalladēva (Vikramāditya VI)
Date
Chāḷukya Vik-rama year 4, Siddhārthin, Jyēshṭha, śu. 10, Thursday and Chāḷukya Vikrama year 11, Kshaya, Uttarāyaṇa-Saṅkrānti.
Language
Kanarese
Remarks
States that when the Mahāmaṇḍalēśvara Jōyimayya-rasa was ruling the Sindavāḍi-one-thousand province his officer Perggaḍe [Kambaṇa], built the temple of Kambēśvara and got a grant of land made to it at the capital town of Tumbuḷa. Mentions the tank Jōyiyasamudra, the rājaguru Sōmaśiva-Paṇḍita, and the districts Eḍedoṟe-two-thousand, Kailakeḷage five-hundred and Moṟaṭa three-hundred.
ARIE/1915-1916/B/1915/520 (page 50)
Placement
On a slab lying on the tank-bund in the same village.
Dynasty
Yādava
King
Jaitugi (I)
Date
Śaka 1[151], Virōdhin, Chaitra, śuddha 10, Wednes-day.
Language
Sanskṛit & Kanarese
Remarks
Mentions the minister Murāri-Kēśava. Records that the god Yōgamūrti Narasiṁhadēva was established on the western side of the Joyya-tank at Tumbuḷa or Hiṟiya-Tumbuḷa in the Sindhuvāṭi country and that the mahājanas of that village made a grant of land for worship and offerings.

ARIE/1915-1916/B/1915/555 (page 54)
Placement
On a slab set up at the entrance into the village of Malakapuram.
Dynasty
Western Chāḷuk-ya.
King
Traiḷōkyamalla Bhujabaḷa Vīra Rāyamurāri Sōmēśvaradēva (IV), ruling from Jayantī-pura.
Date
Śaka 1106, Krō-dhin, Kārttika, New-moon (Āmāvāsyē). Monday, solar eclipse.
Language
Kanarese (verse & prose)
Remarks
Evidently the slab belongs to the village of Pedda Tumbalam. Gives a genealogical account of the chiefs Brahma (Bammidēva), his son Padmidēva and Vatsarāja the maternal uncle of the latter. Padmidēvarasa and Vatsarāja were ruling the whole of the eastern country including Sindavāḍi. The village Kantarike in Bāgi 12, a sub-division of Sindavāḍi-one-thousand, was granted to the temple of Brahmēśvaradēva (at Kaṟekaṇṭhapura in Kīrtinārāyaṇapura, the capital of the Sindavāḍi province) which had been built by the merchant Śrōtriya Eṟeyama-seṭṭi.

On a pillar set up in front of the Vīra-bhadrasvāmin temple in the same village.
Dynasty
Vijayanagara
King
Vīrapratāpa Vīra-Kṛishṇādēva-Mahārāya
Date
Sarvajit(=Śaka 1449-50), Āshā-ḍha, śuddha [6], Śivarātri (?).
Language
Kanarese
Remarks
Gift of land by Suṅkaṇa-Nāyaka, son of Dāḍi-Nāyaka to the temple of Pēṭe-Vīrabhadradēva of Keṟe-Beḷugallu (included in Ādavani-durga) which was granted to him as amara by the king.
ARIE/1915-1916/B/1915/560 (page 55)
Placement
On the Jaina image of Vardhamānasvāmin (now worshipped as a Hindu idol) at Kammarchodu (Alur taluk, Bellary district).
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
…
Language
Kanarese (verse & prose)
Remarks
In characters of about the 12th century A.D. Registers the reconsecration (of this image) by Chandavve the wife of the merchant chief (mahā-vaḍḍavyavahāri) Rāyara-seṭṭi who was the favourite pupil of Padmaprabha-Maladhārisvāmin.
ARIE/1915-1916/B/1915/561 (page 55)
Placement
On a slab set up in the court-yard of the Bhōgēsvara temple in the same village.
Dynasty
Western Chāḷu-kya.
King
Traiḷōkyamalladēva (Sōmēśvara I), ruling from Kampile.
Date
Śaka 976, Jaya, Paushya śuddha 1[5], Sunday, Uttarāyaṇa-Saṅkrānti, lunar eclipse.
Language
Kanarese
Remarks
Gift of land by certain gāvuṇḍas, to the temples of Mūlasthānadēva and Bhōgēśvaradēva at Kamma-[ra]cheṟuvu while the Mahāmaṇḍalēśvara Vīra-Noḷamba-Gaṭṭidēva of the Pattava family was ruling the Sindavāḍi-one-thousand.
ARIE/1915-1916/B/1915/562 (page 55)
Placement
On a pillar set up in a field at Hulibidu (same taluk and district).
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
4th year, Sarvajit
Language
Kanarese
Remarks
Mutilated at the top. Registers the death of a hero named Siriguppa when the latter opposed on behalf of the Raṭṭas the army of Dantiga, which attacked the village Chīkurambrāvi.
ARIE/1915-1916/B/1915/563 (page 55)
Placement
On a slab set up in the court-yard of the Jōtinātha temple at Joti (Sidhout taluk, Cuddapah district).
Dynasty
…
King
Rakkasa-Gaṅgarasadēva-Mahāraja
Date
Śaka 1169, Plavaṅga, Jyēshṭha, śuddha, 13 (trayōdasī), Saturday.
Language
Telugu
Remarks
Registers that Chenti Rāmi-Nāyaka, the servant of the Mahāmaṇḍalēśvara Rayidēva-Mahārāja, built the compound wall and the gōpura of the temple of Jōtinātha. He also constructed a temple for Irugalasāni at Takaprōlu and made other gifts at Cheṭlūru.
ARIE/1915-1916/B/1915/564 (page 55)
Placement
At the entrance, on the east wall of the old fort at Sidhout (same taluk and district).
Dynasty
Vijayanagara
King
Vīra-Veṅkaṭarāya, ruling the Chandragiri-sīma.
Date
Śaka 1527, Viśva-vasu.
Language
Sanskṛit & Telugu (verse)
Remarks
Registers that this stone fort was extended (?) by the Maṭli chief Ananta of the solar race whose father Ellamarāja conquered Siddhavaṭa after fighting the battle of Ūṭukūru.
ARIE/1915-1916/B/1915/565 (page 55)
Placement
On a slab set up on the Kailāsappa-guṭṭa (hill) at Konakondla (Gooty taluk, Anantapur district).
Dynasty
Western Chāḷu-kya.
King
Tribhuvanamalladēva (Vikramāditya VI), ruling from Poṭṭaḷakeṟe.
Date
Chāḷukya Vik-rama year 6, Durmati, Pushya, bahuḷa [6], Thursday, Uttarāyaṇa-Saṅkrānti.
Language
Kanarese
Remarks
Records that Nāvikabbe built a Jaina temple called Chaṭṭa-Jinālaya at Koṇḍakundeyatīrtha and [her husband] the Mahāmaṇḍalēśvara Jōyimayyarasa who was entitled Pēśaṇa-Garuḍa gave 30 mattar of black-soil land at Kiṟiya Koṇḍakunde, to that temple.
ARIE/1915-1916/B/1915/566 (page 55)
Placement
On a slab lying in a field near the same village.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Tribhuvanamalladēva (Vikramāditya VI)
Date
Chāḷukya Vikrama year 12, Vibhava, Uttarāyaṇa-Saṅkrānti.
Language
Kanarese
Remarks
Damaged. Mentions first the Mahāmaṇḍalēśvara Ballaya-Chōḷa-Mahārāja who was ruling the Sinda-vāḍi-one-thousand province and whose praśasti begins with the words Charaṇa-sarōruha, etc.; then it mentions the Mahāmaṇḍalēśvara Chīkarasa of the Mahābali race whose praśasti begins with the words Jagattrayābhivandita, etc., and next the Mahā-sāmantas Chandarasa, Barmmarasa and Rēvarasa of Koṇḍakunde, whose praśasti begins with the words ari-durdhara, etc., seems to record the grant of a land.

ARIE/1915-1916/B/1915/582 (page 57)
Placement
On the same wall
Dynasty
Do.
King
Māṟavarman alias [Tribhu]vana[cha]kra-vartin Sundara-Pāṇḍyadēva, ‘who was pleased to distribute the Chōḷa country.’
Date
13th year
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Records that as there was no money in the treasury of the temple of Piṇakkaṟutta-Nāyaṉār in Malaiyaḍikkuṟichchi, the southern hamlet of Pirāntaka-chaturvēdimaṅgalam a brahmadēya in Āri-nāḍu, a certain Puliyūr-kiḻavaṉ Piraḷaya-Viḍaṅgan Abhayampukkāṉ living in the street called Kulaśēkharapperunderu, defrayed the expenses to be met in regard to the tax called vini-yōgam on the tank Ulaguyyavanda-Pāṇḍyappērēri and made a gift of his right to one-third of the income from the tank along with some money to the temple, for offerings to Tiruppaḷḷiyarai-Nāchchiyār and Tukkaiyār. Mentions the temple of Tirukkaḻanīśvaramuḍaiya-Nāyanār at Savadam-paṭṭakurichchi which belonged to the tantirattār i.e. the Kaikkōḷas the Sēnāpat is and Daṇḍanāyakas.
ARIE/1915-1916/B/1915/583 (page 57)
Placement
On the north and west walls of the same maṇḍapa.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Jaṭilavarman alias Tribhuvanacha[kravar-tin] Kōnērmaikoṇḍān Tirunelvēipperu-māḷ. born under the asterism A[śva]ti in Vaigāśi.
Date
Śaka 1457, Man-matha, Kārt-tigai, 23, śu. di. 12, Mon-day, Śōbhana-yōga, Svāti.
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Gift of land to a number of persons of various gōtras and sūtras. Records that these lands and the tank called Mānābharaṇappērēri included in Āri-nāḍu, were now joined to the village of Abhirāma-Parākramapāṇḍiya-chaturvēdimaṅgalam. They were divided into 10 shares and given to 11 persons. Mentions the king's father (āchchaṉ ?) Āhava-rāman Śrīvaladēva.

ARIE/1915-1916/B/1915/607 (page 60)
Placement

Date
3rd year
Language
Tamil (about the 12th century A.D.).
Remarks
Introduction commences with the words pUmakaL jayamakaL. Registers a gift of land by the king to the temple of Piṇakkaṟukku-Mahādēva at Malai-yaḍikkurichchi, the southern hamlet of Parān-taka-chaturvēdimaṅgalam, a brahmadēya in Āri-nāḍu. When ordering the grant, the king was in his palace at Tirunelvēli in Kīḻvēmba-nāḍu. Mentions Vīrapāṇḍiyan Pilāṟu and the seat called Muṉaiyadaraiyaṉ. Below this is an incomplete record dated in the 11th year, probably, of the same king.

ARIE/1915-1916/B/1915/615 (page 61)
Placement
On the same rock
Dynasty
Pāṇḍya
King
Danma-Perumāḷ Aḷagapperumāḷ Ativīrarā-maṉ Śīvala-Māṟaṉ Irandakālameḍutta Ativīrarāmaṉ.

Language
Tamil
Remarks
Registers a sarvamānya grant of land to three private individuals. The grant was issued during the reign of Veṅkaṭapatirāya of Vijayanagar whose ancestors Dēvarāya, Kṛishṇarāya, Sadāśiva-rāya, Vīra-Narasiṁharāya, Dharmarāya and Śrīraṅgarāya are mentioned at the commencement of the record with a string of birudas as in No. 614 above. The rock on which the inscription is engraved is called Ūśippāṟai at Taṭṭāṉkiṇaṟu.

Remarks
Registers a gift of gold by Viṇṇagōvaraiyar to (the temple of ?) Kuṉṟanār-Baṭṭāri worshipped by Viṇṇakōvaraiyar, for the merit Udāraḍi and Nambi... who fell in a cattle-raid. The gold was received by the residents of Kīḻvaḻi-Aruvāgūr in Śiṅgapura-nāḍu.
ARIE/1915-1916/C/1916/284 (page 92)
Placement
On a pillar in the rock-cut cave at Melaich-cheri (same taluk and district).
Dynasty
Pallava
King
Chanrdāditya
Date
…
Language
Pallava-Grantha
Remarks
States that this (rock-cut) Śiva temple called Śrī-Śikhari-Pallavēśvaram, was excavated by king Chandrāditya at Siṅha (Siṁha)pura.
